text:
Fabulous!  I had some sour cream and very ripe bananas to use up, so I tried this recipe.  So glad I did!  Both the banana and chocolate flavors came through.  Modifications:  1) Used regular sour cream and mini chocolate chips because that's what I had on hand.  With mini chocolate chips, chocolate flavor is more evenly distributed.  Since my bananas were small, I used 7.  2) Whisked dry ingredients (flour, baking soda, and cocoa powder) together in one bowl and created a hole in the middle.  In another bowl, mixed the wet ingredients (margarine, white sugar, eggs, mashed bananas, and vanilla extract).  Then poured the wet mixture and sour cream in the middle of the dry ingredients and mixed by hand until just incorporated.  Finally, stirred in the chips.  This method will prevent tough bread.  3) Instead of two big loaves, I made 8 mini loaves with the batter and baked them for 35 minutes.  Less time and easier to share with friends.  This tastes more like a loaf cake than traditional banana bread, so this will not replace my tried and true banana nut bread recipe.  However, this will be a wonderful addition to my repertoire, especially when I want to impress guests with an unique homemade baked treat.  *Update on 9/22/06: Made bread with regular semi-sweet chocolate chips and mini chips many time with great success.  Today used white chips, and they dissolved into gooey, sticky mess that stuck to the bottom of the pans and left ugly holes throughout the loaves.

I've been meaning to rate this recipe for a while...let's just say that it's one of my FAVORITE things to bake.  First of all, if you love chocolate, you need to try this.  Second, if you want a spin on traditional banana bread, this is it!  I personally did not find the chocolate overwhelming (you can definitely tell it's banana bread), in fact, I threw in extra chocolate chips!  I also added some walnuts for texture.  The recipe is simple, and quick to throw together...I did extend the baking time a little though.  Try it...you won't regret it!  :)

text:
Just a tip for people who change the recipe -- you won't want to substitute baking powder for the soda (they work in TOTALLY different ways and react with ingredients differently). However, if you use brown sugar, you may want to add a half teaspoon more of the baking soda in order to balance out the extra acid in the brown sugar (brown sugar has molasses added, making it more acidic than white sugar). Just a tip!

I cut the recipe in half and used half white sugar and half brown sugar. It smelled wonderful and tasted even better!

text:
I always read the lowest reviews for a recipe first-that tells me what NOT to do. In this case, I think all the bad reviews may be user error. I too followed the recipe exactly except for the chocolate chips. I also cut the recipe in half to make just one loaf. It was so good, I may throw out my tried and true banana bread recipe I've had for over 5 years. I love banana bread with chocolate chips, this was so much better, with chocolate in every bite. The key with this bread (and any other quick bread calling for butter or margarine) is to cream the butter and sugar for at least 5 minutes. This gives the bread a lighter texture and prevents the dreaded "dense" loaf. Thanks for the recipe and keep 'em comin!

text:
I had a bunch of old bananas to use up-so I decided to stray away from my usual recipe and got funky with this one..I'm so glad I did.  DELICIOUS!  I used butter instead of margarine, 7 or 8 med sized bananas(very ripe ones), 1/2 cup cocoa, regular sour cream(I mean why skimp on fat when there's choc involved),a few more chocolate chips and 3/4 cup walnuts.  I also mixed my sour cream with the baking soda and let that sit a moment to take away the heaviness of the sour cream(it makes it more fluffy)- then added as directed.  I always bake in the disposable aluminum loaf pans(I think breads cook in them the best) and it made four with this batch.  I baked for 53 minutes and they were so moist and perfect.  Thanks so much for sharing this one!

text:
Holy smokes, this is GREAT! Incredible taste and so moist! Some modifications I made: I used butter instead of margarine (I never bake with margarine anyhow); no cocoa powder on hand so just replaced that with flour; half white sugar and half brown sugar; double the amount of chocolate chips. One more thing: I cannot emphasize enough the importance of letting your bananas get overripe for any sort of banana baking. I don't doubt that underripe bananas account for the lack of banana taste that some people have mentioned. Let them ripen - that means completely brown skins! Don't let it scare you :).

The second time I separated the two flavours, and it was the best banana cake I've ever tasted - no joke.  My husband doesn't like banana cake & he even commented it was the best I'd ever made (I've made a lot :-) So, I omitted the cocoa powder entirely, used brown sugar instead of white, added an extra banana & doubled the chocolate (I used dark chocolate chunks).  Oh, and I sprinkled the top with brown sugar before putting it in the oven.  The result was a moist banana cake with gushy chocolate chunks, and a crunchy sugary top.  So good.  It's even better the next day (I warm it in the microwave for a few seconds).  Yumm!  I'll be making this again - alot!

text:
I take baked goods into work quite frequently.  This is BY FAR my most requested recipe!  This is the most moist, yummy bread that I have ever had!  Very easy to prepare, also.  I have used 4-6 bananas (depending on what I have had on hand) and still have come out with great results each time!  
I do have to note, though, that since this is such a dense and moist bread, you MUST use good (aka sturdy, heavy duty) bread pans.  Do NOT try to put this into two small (8x4)loaf pans- they must be the 9x5 pans, otherwise it will not cook properly!  I do not usually cook it all of the way till a toothpick comes out clean, just till it doesn't come out gooey looking!  It will continue to set up after baking and you will have a very moist bread.  Thank you for this recipe!!!

text:
I made this bread yesterday afternoon, and I love it! I followed the recipe pretty much exactly.  Aside from scaling it down to make only one loaf, the only things I did differently were to replace 1/3 of the flour with whole wheat, use mini chocolate chips (I prefer them in breads), and to replace the sour cream with strawberry flavored kefir.  I did the last because I thought I had sour cream but realized too late that I didn't.  Oops.  I used 1/2 c of the kefir, and it turned out fine.  I just had to bake it for an extra 10 min because of the extra moisture.

I also found that heating slices in the microwave for 15-20 sec helps bring out some of the banana flavor, for those who were complaining that the chocolate covered it up.

I made this tonight and all I want to add to the wonderful reviews is that I used whole wheat flour and it still turned out great!  (I try to sneak extra fiber in for us whenever I can)  I didn't tell my husband and he didn't notice the difference.  

I also added about a cup of freeze dried strawberries and walnuts and called it banana split bread.  Although, as many other reviewers have stated, it turns out more like cake than bread.  Moist, wonderful cake.

Great recipe, it adapts well to changes and additions.

text:
Very nice bread!  I will begin by saying that this was neither dominant in the chocolate or the banana flavour, so it was a nice change!  I made a few modifications as I typically do with any muffins/loaves, but I am sure this loaf does not need changing.  I just like to cut some calories and fat if I can!  That said, I only used one egg with 5 whites (had a carton open), 1/4 cup becel along with 3/4 cup unsweetened applesauce, 7 bananas (this is what I use when I make my normal loaf that I double!) and I did not measure my choc chips, just threw in a couple of handfuls of mini (these work best!) semi sweet ones.  I also reduced the sugar to only about 2/3 cup (yes, it's drastic from 2 full cups).  I always find that the overripe bananas add sweetness, as do the choc chips, so to me, 2 cups is way too much, but that's just my opinion!  Will make this again, thanks for the post!

text:
I have used this recipe several times and each time I have been told, "This is the BEST banana bread EVER", "This is the most moist banana bread I have ever tasted", "This bread is amazing"; to name a few. The comments that it is gooey and it takes longer to bake than the directions indicate, should take in account that with any baking there are several variables, oven, altitude, ripeness of the bananas, etc. Use the one hour as a benchmark. I have found it takes between an hour and 1 hour 15 minutes. Don't forget to do the toothpick test. Also, if you don't want chocolate taste in your banana bread. Don't make "Chocolate Banana Bread" and stick with the standard banana bread recipe. If I could give this over 5 stars I would.

I also used a bundt pan but at 350F, my bread was just slightly overcooked at 60 minutes, but slightly undercooked at 45.  So start checking at 45 minutes!  It smelled so amazing that I didn't let it cool long enough before trying to get it out of the pan, so it broke in half, but that was my bad!  However, having the hot gooey chocolate banana mess in a bowl was amazing, and if I weren't lactose intolerant I would have put a little vanilla ice cream on top and been in heaven!  I froze half of the bundt to keep myself from devouring the whole thing in 4 days or something ;)  Will let you know how it defrosts!

text:
I made this bread this morning for something different from your usual banana bread. I make one with a chocolate
cake mix that my husband liked, but I wanted to cut out some of the processed flavor.
I cut this recipe in half to make one loaf. I omitted the chocolate chips (I didn't have any) and used light vanilla yogurt. I was pleased at how nicely this cooked up, it wasn't wet like some banana breads can be. (Like the outside will cook quicker than the inside and you have a half-done banana bread.) This 
made my whole house smell wonderful. 

I plan on frosting it with the Mocha Icing from this site and leaving it out
for my husband when he gets home. I'll
update how it blows over with him.

EDITED: This bread is my-tee-fine. Really moist and flavorful. And even better with the Mocha Glaze. I wouldn't 
make it every day, but it's yummy every once in a while.

I found this recipe and made it last night.  I was somewhat nervous considering all the vast reviews, but I'm very glad I tried.  This "bread" (I call it cake) is absolutely delicious.  I made a couple of changes.  I only used 1 1/2 cups of sugar (and so glad I did) and used low-fat vanilla yogurt instead of the sour cream. I also do everything by hand, so it took me well over 10 minutes to prepare it, but I placed it in a 13X9 inch baking pan and it was done at 45 minutes.  Can't wait to go grab another piece now. It is sweet, but not sickenly so.  I highly recommend it.

text:
Easy on the liquid if you are using frozen bananas.  The bread is excellent but I feel the mixture is on the edge of too wet - if you are using your 6 bananas from the freezer, defrost them and drain extra liquid out of the bowl they defrosted in - otherwise your bread may not bake through.  I am not a walnut lover, but I have found I do like the bread better with 2 cups of crushed walnuts (maybe it's that 'something' that some say is missing).   Haven't tried adding salt - I feel it turns out fine without it (and I use unsalted igredients).

text:
I've been searching for the ultimate banana bread recipe, and after trying about six from this site, this recipe has proved to be head and shoulders above the rest! It is so moist and dense, yet it bakes up high in the pan. So many of the other recipes turned out to be squat little loaves. I left the chocolate chips out, and it still had a nice deep cocoa flavor. Our family loves nuts in everything, but this recipe is perfect without any add-ins - the texture is that good. I doubt I'll bother to bake any other kind of banana bread again. It makes two generous loaves of heavenly bread.

Fantastic. I used extremely ripe bananas, so I didn't notice an overpowering chocolate taste at all; there was a great balance between the two flavors. The only changes to the recipe were to halve it, substitute butter for margarine, and use regular sour cream. Due to my limited pan selection, I had to use an 8x4. This turned out just fine after I omitted what I thought was an appropriate amount of batter for the pan size. I found this single, slightly smaller loaf was completely cooked after about 50 minutes. This recipe was a success and I would most definitely make it again!

text:
This tastes really really good for a chocolate cake/bread, but it doesn't satisfy the urge for the banana bread my Nana used to make.  As a chocolate lover, I loved this recipe.  I read the reviews, and the cooking time was off for me, too.  To avoid burning, I baked at 325 for 1 hour 20 min., and it came out perfectly. I HIGHLY recommend using a high quality cocoa powder (like Scharfenberger)... if you use Hershey's or something like that then you won't get the rich, chocolately taste. It really makes a difference!

This is one of my goto recipes. Unless there's a dietary restriction, I'm morally against all things 'light' and have always used full fat sour cream. If you have bananas that aren't ripe enough to bake with, they can be put in the oven (at the lowest temp) for an hour or so and pull them out when black.

Mmmmm... this is good!  I made a lot of modifications, and the texture was a little off, but certainly my fault and not the recipe's.  I replaced one cup of flour with quinoa flour, only used 1 cup of sugar, and replaced the eggs with 4 T flax meal soaked in 8 T water. I will be making this again next time I have overripe bananas. Thanks!

These are SO good!! I did make some changes due to ingredients I had on hand. I used butter, b/c I never use margarine. I did 1 cup white sugar and 1 cup brown sugar. I did a heaping 1/4 cup of cocoa powder. I did half sour cream and half FF vanilla yogurt b/c that's all I had. I also added 1 tsp cinnamon and 1 tsp salt. I also added 1 1/2 cups mini chocolate chips. I baked these in a mini muffin tin for 13 mins. I used my little cookie scoop to fill muffin tins. They are SO yummy! I will be making this often!

I have probably made this every week for 2 months, I just love it!  I've made a few alterations: I've added up to 8 bananas...just whatever I have on hand.  I use dark chocolate chips, instead of semi-sweet, and put a little over half the bag in, so maybe more like 1.5 cups.  I also add in a cup or so of chopped pecans. Probably closer to 1 hr 20 minutes, even in a convection oven.

I CHANGED THIS RECIPE A LITTLE AND I GOT RAVES FROM MY COWORKERS WHEN I SHARED A LOAF WITH THEM.  Prior to making this recipe the first time, I read the first page of reviews.  I too wondered if the ingredient of salt had been erroneously omitted so added 1/2 tsp. of salt to my SINGLE loaf recipe the FIRST TIME I baked this banana bread.  As I was assembling my ingredients, I realized I didnâ€™t have any unsweetened cocoa powder but I did have a box of Hersheyâ€™s all natural unsweetened bakers chocolate bars.  I added 2 bars/oz. to a stick of butter, (I never use margarine), and melted them very slowly together over the simmer burner on my gas stove turned all the way down in a stainless steel mixing bowl.  I added the sugar to the butter cocoa mixture and once this cooled down I added the eggs.  I also used regular sour cream and added a cup of chopped walnuts and instead of 1/2 c. of chocolate chips, I added 3/4 c. Ambrosia semisweet chocolate chips that can be purchased at Costco in a 6 lb. bag, (Iâ€™m a serious chocoholic).  I felt the loaf was just a bit too chocolaty because you could barely taste the bananas.  Everyone asked me what kind of cake it was.
The SECOND time I made this SINGLE loaf recipe I added 1 tsp. of salt, 1.5 oz. of Hersheyâ€™s all natural unsweetened bakers chocolate bars, 1 c. of the Ambrosia semisweet chocolate chips and 1/2 c. of chopped pecanâ€™s.  I like the second version a little better but both versions were very good.

text:
Some have said that there is not much banana flavor, which is true. This is not your classic banana bread. It has a rich, moist chocolate flavor.

I have made this recipe three times now. It is definitely a keeper, and I continue to tinker with it.

The first time I made it, I had to bake the 8-cup loaves for 1 hour 15 minutes, vs. the 1 hour that the recipe indicated. Even after the additional time in the oven, there was a fudgy streak in the center of the loaf. I know my refrigerator is colder than most. Maybe the sour cream and eggs were too cold, increasing the bake time. I used full fat sour cream.

The second time I made it, I halved the recipe, keeping the cocoa powder the same (1/4 cup). I divided the dough into two 4-cup loaf pans, and the bake time was still 60 minutes, despite the smaller loaves. I also added 1/2 cup chopped walnuts. This time, the loaves were perfect. I prefer smaller loaves anyway.

If you follow my changes and additions, you will probably need to reduce the bake time to 45 minutes. This is just a guess.

text:
This tastes good, but it seems more like chocolate cake than a banana bread. The chocolate in this quick bread overpowers the taste of bananas, though. I did use full size chocolate chips, not the minis.  Maybe the minis would be better for this recipe? You must let this quick bread bake for a full 70 minutes or it will not be done on the inside.  Test it with a cake tester before you remove it from the oven.  If it's not done, retest it in 5 minutes intervals until the cake tester comes out clean of banana batter (melted chocolate is okay on the tester).   I used regular sour cream and the results were fine.

text:
This was a good recipe although not as good as I expected from the other reviews.  I was concerned that it would be too chocolaty, but in fact I will probably increase the chips to 1 1/2 or 2 cups next time.  Mine had a very prominent banana flavor, and I wonder if those who didn't maybe didn't use ripe enough bananas.  It was not, however, as good a flavor as I get in my usual banana bread recipe.  As for the chocolate flavor, if the loaves weren't brown I wouldn't have even know it was there.  I plan on incorporating more of my usual banana bread recipe into this one as well as adding more chocolate chips and maybe even more cocoa, and with that I hope to get a really delicious bread.

text:
Amazing! I halfed the recipe, and made it in one 10x6 pan for 45 minutes. 
DIRECTIONS/INGREDIENTS:
1. I mixed dry ingredients first, with one sub and a couple additions: 1/2 cup brown sugar, 1/2 cup white sugar, 1.5 cups flour, 1 tsp baking soda, 2 tablespoons cacao powder, + dash of sea salt, + cinnamon. 
2. I made a well in the center, and added in wet ingredients AFTER I mixed them in a separate bowl: 2 eggs, only TWO bananas, 1 tsp vanilla extract, 1/2 cup melted butter, 1/2 cup regular (non-lite) sour cream, + ~2 tablespoons of milk for texture to compensate for the lack of a third banana. 
3. Added about 1/2 cup mini semi-sweet chocolate chips. This spread the chocolatey-ness a bit better throughout the bread. I also used about 1/4 cup to sprinkle on top of the batter.
RESULTS: Delicious! I still taste plenty of banana, and the chocolate is not overwhelming. I'll make it just like this next time :)

text:
This was a good basic recipe.  If you start out w/ room temp butter and eggs, and get a really fluffy creaming going on, and don't over mix after that,  the rest falls into place for a nice texture and rise to the final product.  I tweaked the recipe for my personal taste (yogurt instead of sour cream, extra milk-choc. chips along w/ the semi-sweet, about 1/4c extra cocoa powder because I wanted a richer choc. and less banana flavor, nuts, 1TBSP espresso powder in the banana to darken the flavor, a dash of cinnamon).  None of my tweaks should make a difference to the success of the final product as written, it's a good, solid recipe in my opinion.  If you are looking for a slight variation, try my little changes!

text:
Moist and very good, I will definitely make this again. Entire family ate it up. Chose this because it was chocolate and also because no nuts (both my kids have nut allergies) and because it uses a larger quantity of bananas and I had 6 brown ones sitting on the counter.  I made the following changes: 1) had no margarine so used butter  2) replaced all the sugar with 1/2 c brown sugar Splenda baking blend and I could have even reduced that to 1/3 c - will do that next time.  3) used fat free sour cream   4) baked the entire batch in a classic bundt pan.  

Because of my ingredient changes, it flattened slightly while cooling (but kept its nice bundt shape overall). No one cared after it was sliced! Great recipe. Makes lots of cake.

text:
Was great! Going to be my go-to banana bread recipe. 

Didn't have sour cream so I used mayonnaise. Worked out really well. Not sure what the sour cream is supposed to do for the recipe anyway, but the mayo gave it that bit of extra moisture and the whole thing was insanely moist and dense in a great way. 

Second time made muffins -- albeit without the cocoa powder, since I just wanted straight up banana muffins. Used brown sugar just to test. To see if it would make any kind of difference, and as far as I could tell, it did not.  Worked out really well still.

All in all it is a great recipe! Very versatile.

text:
Chocoholics, this one's for you! It is chocolately! YUM!! However, next time, I'll either add more banana or use less cocoa powder because the chocolate flavor overwhelmed the banana to the point where I couldn't taste the banana! I'll also omit the mini chocolate chips, unless they start making them in milk chocolate. (The semisweet ones are a bit too bitter for my taste.) I made just a few minor changes. I cut the recipe in half as I wanted only one loaf. I used one-quarter cup butter and one-quarter cup unsweetened applesauce, and I used about a half cup of regular sour cream, which made the bread wonderfully moist. Bake for about 90 minutes. I will definitely make this again! :^) (P.S. Eat this with peanut butter spread on top of the slice!)

text:
I thought this tasted alright. It did seem more like a soft chocolate cake than banana bread tasting in taste or texture.  However, I also made some changes to make it a based on what I had in the house. I made 1/2 recipe, used butter instead of margarine. Part oil would have been fine too. I had to sub non fat Greek plain yogurt for the sour cream and did 1/3 of the flour, or 1/2 cup, as white whole wheat. With a full cup of sugar, I opted to just sprinkle approximately 3 tablespoons of mini chocolate chips on top. To up the chocolate flavor I doubled the unsweet cocoa powder. It seemed like way too much batter for 1 loaf. So, I chose to make muffins. I got 18 muffins.  They took 23 minutes to bake in a greased muffin tin.

text:
We gave this recipe 5 stars for the idea because we changed it quite a bit. Added one 5.6 oz cup of lemon whipped greek yogurt and changed the margarin to 3/4 stick of butter. For the sugar, changed it to 3/4 cup white sugar and 2/3 cup agave nectar. We then used one 5.6 oz cup of lime whipped greek yogurt in place of the sour cream. Poured the batter into a cupcake pan and cut the cooking time in half (30 min). Finally, used half dark chocolate chips. The changes were made to attempt to make a healthier version and it really worked. Loving them!

text:
Excellent recipe that makes great moist muffins too! The only change I made is I used regular sour cream, rest of ingredients same.  Still bake at 350, but 25-30 mins (for convection ovens closer to 25 mins).  Place (Reynolds) baking cups in cupcake/muffin tins.  Fill muffin cups 3/4 full.  Yields 30(+) muffins.  Easy fill tip:  Put batter in gallon ziploc and cut off very tip of one bottom end.  Squeeze batter through tip into cups.  *If you have an icing bag tip, put tip in corner before batter for more stability.

I kept this one to myself, I told my employees about it but I could not part with it. It kept great covered on the counter (4 days). Very moist, chocolate was not overpowering (maybe because I added 8 bananas). Def a keeper! Thanks Tracie.

This bread is very yummy.  Used butter instead of margarine, 2 1/2 cups flour instead of 3, (2 cups wheat flour and 1/2 all pur-purpose) and up the cocoa to 1/2 cup. I used yoghurt instead of sour cream and I mixed it with the mashed bananas I guess to avoid it getting darker. Also added 1/2 tsp salt, 1 tsp cinnamon and 1 cup of raisins instead of choc chips. Very yummy.

This is a good recipe. I don't quite understand all the hype about them being to chocolatey?? Mine tastes like banana bread with chocolate chips...nothing more or less. For those of you who want to double the recipe be sure you have a very very big bowl and the mixing power to mix it. I doubled it and my hubby was laughing at me as I had to use a huge pasta pot to mix it all up in and I also needed his help and I am not a whimp at all lol. I made two loaves and one round cake pan and a dozen muffins. I took the others advice and also increased the baking time and I think one hour would have been sufficent enough. Over-all god recipe but I will continue my mission to find my staple banana bread. Thanx

text:
Excellent banana bread recipe! Very moist, and not an overpowering banana OR chocolate flavor. I followed it almost exactly - my only changes were to use unsalted butter instead of margarine, so I added a tsp. of salt, and I didn't have quite a cup of lite sour cream left, so filled up the rest of the cup with nonfat vanilla yogurt. I made 12 regular sized muffins, one mini loaf and one big loaf! This is a BIG recipe, so either halve it if you don't want a lot of bread/muffins, or make sure to use a really big bowl! Next time I may add a tsp. of cinnamon, I think that would be great with this combination of flavors. Thanks for the recipe!

text:
A classic chocolate banana bread.  Has that spreadable banana-bread texture, but it's as rich and chocolatey as a cake - I bet that caused the cake-like complaints (you could spread something on it, but you won't want to).  Used exact ingredients (though any sour cream would be fine) but I combined the dry seperately, creamed margarine & sugar then added eggs, then bananas & vanilla, then the dry, sour cream and chocolate chips all at once (that's the way most muffin & bread recipes I've seen work).  Can bake as 24 muffins for about 30 minutes if you're in a rush or want a more portable treat.  Also, I bet adding 1/4 cup cocoa powder or subbing it for 1/4 cup flour would make your favorite b. bread recipe into a good chocolate b. bread if you add a bit extra sugar (1/4 c?).

This is an awesome treat! I made it with mini chocolate chips and since I had no butter on hand I used shortening with a few tablespoons of water. The recipe made 1 regular loaf, 9 mini loaves, and 24 mini muffins. It was very moist and fluffy. The family loved it. Next time I will experiment with lowering the fat in the recipe (egg whites, half margarine/half applesauce, etc.). I highly recommend mini chocolate chips because they don't over-power it like the regular sized chips do.
